tips for SaaS founders who don\u2019t want VC money"},"content":{"rendered":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Aytekin Tank<\/span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor<\/span>\n\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"contributor__twitter\">\n\t\t\t<a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/aytekintank\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<svg class=\"icon icon--twitter icon--white\" viewBox=\"0 0 20 20\" version=\"1.1\" aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter<\/title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"\/>\t<\/svg>\n\t\t\t\t<\/a>\n\t\t<\/div>\n\t\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tAytekin Tank is the founder of <a href=\"https:\/\/www.jotform.com\/\">JotForm<\/a>, an online form builder. Established in 2006, JotForm allows customizable data collection for enhanced lead generation, survey distribution, payment collections and more.\t<\/div>\n\t\n\t<\/div>\n<\/div><p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Over the past<\/span> decade, venture capital has become synonymous with entrepreneurship. Founders from around the world arrive in Silicon Valley with visions of record-setting A rounds and billion-dollar valuations. But what if you don\u2019t have unicorn dreams \u2014 or you don\u2019t want to pursue VC money?<\/p>\n<p>Bootstrapping a SaaS company is not only possible \u2014 I believe it\u2019s a saner, more sustainable way to build and scale a business. To be clear, bootstrapping isn\u2019t always easy. It requires patience and focus, but the freedom to create a meaningful product, on your terms, is worth more than even the biggest VC check.<\/p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--left\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tThe freedom to create a meaningful product, on your terms, is worth more than even the biggest VC check.\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">I started my company,<\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/www.jotform.com\/\"> JotForm<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">, in 2006. We\u2019ve grown steadily from a simple web tool into a product that serves more than 8 million users \u2014 without taking a dime in outside funding. We\u2019re profitable in an industry with big-name competitors like Google.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Most importantly, I still love this company and its mission, and I want the same for my fellow entrepreneurs. If you\u2019re a SaaS founder who\u2019s wary of VC funding, here are my best bootstrapping tips.<\/p>\n<h2>Keep your day job<\/h2>\n<p>Success stories from founders who leap blindly into business without resources or relevant experience are compelling, but they\u2019re the exception, not the rule. Working inside another organization can build your skills, your network and even inspire great product ideas.<\/p>\n<p>After finishing college with a computer science degree, I worked as a developer for a New York media company. The editors always needed custom web forms, which were tedious and time consuming to build. I kept thinking, \u201cThere has to be a better way.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>That daily frustration led me to start JotForm \u2014 but I didn\u2019t leave my job right away. I stayed with the media firm for five years and worked on my product on the side. By the time I was ready to go all in, I had the confidence, experience and savings I needed.<\/p>\n<p>Many of the world\u2019s biggest companies began as side projects, including Twitter, Craigslist, Slack, Instagram, Trello, and a little venture called Apple. If your day job doesn\u2019t pay enough to fund the early stages of your business, consider a side gig or consulting work. There are so many ways to set yourself up for success without the pressure of VC cash or selling a chunk of your business.<\/p>\n<h2>Know you\u2019re not alone<\/h2>\n<p>The exact numbers shift every year, but data compiled by<a href=\"https:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/230011\"> Fundable<\/a> show that only 0.05% of U.S. startups are backed by VCs. Another 0.91% are funded by angel investors. The vast majority, at 57%, are funded by credit and personal loans, while 38% get funding from friends and family.<\/p>\n<p>It may feel like most founders raise multimillion-dollar rounds, but that\u2019s simply not the case. It\u2019s also good to remember that securing VC money is complicated and time consuming. You can spend months taking meetings and presenting the perfect deck \u2014 and still leave empty handed. Be patient and stick to your own path.<\/p>\n<h2>Measure profits, not popularity<\/h2>\n<p>SaaS founders often emphasize vanity metrics, like user acquisitions and total downloads. These numbers can measure short-term popularity, but they don\u2019t reveal how users and customers feel about your product \u2014 or your long-term potential.<div to expect tomorrow at TC Sessions: Justice 2021"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Get ready to engage in essential conversations about some of the most important issues facing the tech industry \u2014 diversity, equity, inclusion and labor. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/\">TC Sessions: Justice 2021<\/a> \u2014 a day-long virtual symposium \u2014 begins tomorrow, March 3, and we\u2019re here to highlight just a few of the powerful people, presentations and fireside chats you won\u2019t want to miss.<\/p>\n<p>Hold up \u2014 if you don\u2019t have a ticket yet, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#tickets\">secure your seat here<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>You\u2019ll hear from top experts, leading voices and social justice warriors \u2014 from the tech industry and beyond. It\u2019s a highly interactive day, and the virtual platform lets you engage in the conversations, ask questions and connect with participants around the world.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Here are just a few of tomorrow\u2019s compelling presentations and exciting events. You\u2019ll find a complete listing of the day\u2019s programming in the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#1fa16903-b3ec-435b-ba68-d43e00bd8d70\">event agenda<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Creating Equity in Tech with Congresswoman Barbara Lee (D-CA):<\/strong> When it comes to myths, lack of tech diversity as a \u201cpipeline problem\u201d is a whopper. Don\u2019t miss our discussion with Congresswoman Lee, California\u2019s East Bay representative, about the opportunities to create an equal playing field in tech so that underrepresented investors, founders, designers and coders can reap the benefits.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Fireside Chat &#8211; Diversity Is More Than Hiring People of Color:<\/strong> It may appear that the country is accepting change \u2014 from racial diversity to equality in the workplace. However, we still have ways to go. For example, organizational diversity is still about hiring from diverse talent pools. However, activating the full potential of diversity, equity, and inclusion (DEI) requires more than a \u201cpeople strategy.\u201d Robust and sustainable work in this area requires embedding DEI principles, policies, systems and practices into all parts of the business, including the employee and customer experience, brand culture and overall industry\/corporate citizenship. Sponsored by Onshape.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Pitch Feedback:<\/strong> Join us for a pitch feedback session for select TC Include founders exhibiting at TC Sessions: Justice 2021 and moderated by TechCrunch staff.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Access All Areas &#8211; Designing Accessibility From Day One:<\/strong> This session examines the importance of ensuring accessible product design from the beginning. We\u2019ll ask how the social and medical models of disability influence technological evolution. Integrating the expertise of disabled technologists, makers, investors, scientists and software engineers into your company\u2019s DNA from the very beginning is vital to the pursuit of a functioning and equitable society. And could mean you don\u2019t leave money on the table.<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s just a tiny taste of what to expect tomorrow at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/\">TC Sessions: Justice 2021<\/a>. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#tickets\">Grab a pass<\/a>, check <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#1fa16903-b3ec-435b-ba68-d43e00bd8d70\">the agenda<\/a>, plan your day accordingly and join us for the important work of creating a more diverse, inclusive and equitable tech 2021","slug":"tc-sessions-justice-2021","taxonomy":"tc_event","rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/576821871"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_event"}],"up":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/449559507"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_event=576821871"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_events?tc_event=576821871"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tc_event=576821871"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":2119683,"date":"2021-03-02T08:39:21","date_gmt":"2021-03-02T16:39:21","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119683"},"modified":"2021-03-02T16:56:41","modified_gmt":"2021-03-03T00:56:41","slug":"uber-spins-out-delivery-robot-startup-as-serve-robotics","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/uber-spins-out-delivery-robot-startup-as-serve-robotics\/","title":{"rendered":"Uber spins out delivery robot startup as Serve Robotics"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Postmates X, the robotics division of the on-demand delivery startup that\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/01\/uber-officially-completes-postmates-acquisition\/\">Uber acquired last year for $2.65 billion<\/a>, has officially spun out as an independent company called Serve Robotics.<\/p>\n<p>TechCrunch <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/15\/uber-planning-to-spin-out-postmates-delivery-robot-arm\/\">reported in January<\/a> that a deal was being shopped to investors.<\/p>\n<p>Serve Robotics, a name taken from the autonomous sidewalk delivery bot that was developed and piloted by Postmates X, has raised seed funding in a round led by venture capital firm Neo. Other investors included Uber as well as Lee Jacobs and Cyan Banister&#8217;s Long Journey Ventures, Western Technology Investment, Scott Banister, Farhad Mohit and Postmates co-founders Bastian Lehmann and Sean Plaice.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Serve Robotics didn&#8217;t share specifics of the funding except to confirm that the round, which will be a Series A, has not been completed yet. Funding a spin out can occur in phases, with the first tranche used for the initial launch and the rest of the round closing once IP has been transferred.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MFz0gIozAr\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/15\/uber-planning-to-spin-out-postmates-delivery-robot-arm\/\">Uber planning to spin out Postmates&#8217; delivery robot arm<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Uber planning to spin out Postmates&#8217; delivery robot arm&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/15\/uber-planning-to-spin-out-postmates-delivery-robot-arm\/embed\/#?secret=MFz0gIozAr\" data-secret=\"MFz0gIozAr\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The new company will be run by Ali Kashani, who headed up Postmates X. Other co-founders include Dmitry Demeshchuk, the first engineer who joined the Serve team at Postmates and MJ Chun, who previously led product at Anki and has been heading up product strategy at Serve. The company is launching with 60 employees with headquarters in San Francisco and offices in Los Angeles and Vancouver, Canada.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119707\" style=\"width: 810px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119707\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2119707 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg\" alt=\"Serve Robotics Uber Postmates\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg 800w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Serve-meets-dog.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119707\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Serve Robotics<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;While self-driving cars remove the driver, robotic delivery eliminates the car itself and makes deliveries sustainable and accessible to all,&#8221; said Kashani, co-founder and CEO of Serve Robotics. &#8220;Over the next two decades, new mobility robots will enter every aspect of our lives &#8212; first moving food, then everything else.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Postmates\u2019 exploration into sidewalk delivery bots began in earnest in 2017 after the company quietly acquired Kashani\u2019s startup Lox Inc. As head of Postmates X, Kashani set out to answer the question: why move two-pound burritos with two-ton cars? Postmates revealed its first Serve autonomous delivery bot in December 2018. A second generation \u2014 with an identical design but different lidar sensors and few other upgrades \u2014 emerged in summer 2019 ahead of its planned commercial launch in Los Angeles.<\/p>\n<p>The company&#8217;s mission to <span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">design, develop and operate delivery robots specialized in navigating sidewalks will continue, albeit with an eye toward expansion. Serve <\/span>will continue its delivery operations in Los Angeles. It plans to ramp up research and development in the San Francisco Bay Area and expand its market reach<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> through new partnerships.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>The spinout is consistent with Uber&#8217;s aim to narrow the focus of its business on ride-hailing and delivery in a push toward profitability. This strategy began to take shape after Uber&#8217;s public market debut in May 2019 and accelerated last year as the COVID-19 pandemic put pressure on the ride-hailing company. Two years ago, Uber had enterprises across the transportation landscape, from ride-hailing and micromobility to logistics, public transit, food delivery and futuristic bets like autonomous vehicles and air taxis. CEO Dara Khosrowshahi has dismantled the everything-but-the-kitchen-sink approach as he pushes the company toward profitability.<\/p>\n<p>In 2020, Uber offloaded shared scooter and bike unit Jump in a complex deal with Lime, sold a\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/02\/uber-sells-500m-stake-in-its-freight-business-as-the-ride-hailing-giant-works-to-conserve-cash\/\">stake worth $500 million<\/a> in its logistics spinoff Uber Freight and rid itself of its autonomous vehicle unit Uber ATG and its air taxi play Uber Elevate. Aurora\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/07\/uber-sells-self-driving-unit-uber-atg-in-deal-that-will-push-auroras-valuation-to-10b\/\">acquired Uber ATG<\/a> in a deal that had a similar structure to the Jump-Lime transaction. Aurora didn\u2019t pay cash for Uber ATG. Instead, Uber handed over its equity in ATG and invested $400 million into Aurora, which gave it a 26% stake in the combined company. In a similarly crafted deal, Uber Elevate was sold to Joby Aviation in December.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"nuBUPHpzeN\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/07\/uber-sells-self-driving-unit-uber-atg-in-deal-that-will-push-auroras-valuation-to-10b\/\">Uber sells self-driving unit Uber ATG in deal that will push Aurora&#8217;s valuation to $10B<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Uber sells self-driving unit Uber ATG in deal that will push Aurora&#8217;s valuation to $10B&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/07\/uber-sells-self-driving-unit-uber-atg-in-deal-that-will-push-auroras-valuation-to-10b\/embed\/#?secret=nuBUPHpzeN\" data-secret=\"nuBUPHpzeN\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Postmates X, the robotics division of the on-demand delivery startup that\u00a0Uber acquired last year for $2.65 billion, has officially spun out as an independent company called Serve Robotics. TechCrunch reported in January that a deal was being shopped to investors. Serve Robotics, a name taken from the autonomous sidewalk delivery bot that was developed and says China-backed hackers are exploiting Exchange zero-days"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Microsoft is warning customers that a new China state-sponsored threat actor is exploiting four previously undisclosed security flaws in Exchange Server, an enterprise email product built by the software giant.<\/p>\n<p>The technology company said Tuesday that it believes the hacking group, which it calls Hafnium, tries to steal information from a broad range of U.S.-based organizations, including law firms and defense contractors, but also infectious disease researchers and policy think tanks.<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft said Hafnium used the four newly discovered security vulnerabilities to break into Exchange email servers running on company networks, granting the attackers to steal data from a victim&#8217;s organization \u2014 such as email accounts and address books \u2014 and the ability to plant malware. When used together, the four vulnerabilities create an attack chain that can compromise vulnerable on-premise servers running Exchange 2013 and later.<\/p>\n<p>Hafnium operates out of China, but uses servers located in the U.S. to launch its attacks, the company said. Microsoft said that Hafnium was the primary threat group it detected using these four new vulnerabilities. <em>(An earlier version of Microsoft&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/on-the-issues\/2021\/03\/02\/new-nation-state-cyberattacks\/\">blog post<\/a> incorrectly said Hafnium was the &#8220;only&#8221; group to exploit the vulnerabilities.)<\/em><\/p>\n<p>Microsoft declined to say how many successful attacks it had seen, but described the number as &#8220;limited.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Patches to fix those four security vulnerabilities are now out, a week earlier than the company&#8217;s typical patching schedule, usually reserved for the second Tuesday in each month.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Even though we\u2019ve worked quickly to deploy an update for the Hafnium exploits, we know that many nation-state actors and criminal groups will move quickly to take advantage of any unpatched systems,&#8221; said Tom Burt, Microsoft\u2019s vice president for customer security.<\/p>\n<p>The company said it has also briefed U.S. government agencies on its findings, but that the Hafnium attacks are not related to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/17\/fireeye-breach-solarwinds-federal-agencies\/\">the SolarWinds-related espionage campaign<\/a> against U.S. federal agencies. In the last days of the Trump administration, the National Security Agency and the FBI said that <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/05\/fbi-nsa-says-hacks-on-us-federal-agencies-likely-russian-in-origin\/\">the SolarWinds campaign<\/a> was &#8220;likely Russian in origin.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"KOWDaGB7FW\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/23\/solarwinds-hackers-targeted-nasa-federal-aviation-administration-networks\/\">SolarWinds hackers targeted NASA, Federal Aviation Administration networks<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;SolarWinds hackers targeted NASA, Federal Aviation Administration networks&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/23\/solarwinds-hackers-targeted-nasa-federal-aviation-administration-networks\/embed\/#?secret=KOWDaGB7FW\" data-secret=\"KOWDaGB7FW\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Microsoft is warning customers that a new China state-sponsored threat actor is exploiting four previously undisclosed security flaws in Exchange Server, an enterprise email product built by the software giant. The technology company said Tuesday that it believes the hacking group, which it calls Hafnium, tries to steal information from a broad range of U.S.-based issues rare apology in India over drama series"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Amazon on Tuesday issued a rare apology to users in India for an original political drama series over allegations that a few scenes in the nine-part mini series hurt religious sentiments of some people in the key overseas market.<\/p>\n<p>The series, called \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/www.imdb.com\/title\/tt11117570\/\">Tandav<\/a>,\u201d has faced criticism from some people in India &#8212; including a few members of the ruling Bhartiya Janata Party &#8212; over its depiction of Hindu gods and goddesses.<\/p>\n<p>In a message titled, \u201cAmazon Prime Video Apologizes,\u201d the American e-commerce group said it \u201cdeeply regrets that viewers considered certain scenes to be objectionable\u201d and that it had either edited those scenes or removed them altogether from the show after hearing concerns from viewers.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe respect our viewers\u2019 diverse beliefs and apologize unconditionally to anyone who felt hurt by these scenes. Our teams follow company content evaluation processes, which we acknowledge need to be constantly updated to better serve our audiences. We will continue to develop entertaining content with partners, while complying with the laws of India and respecting the diversity of culture and beliefs of our audiences.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The show, which stars several top Bollywood actors including Saif Ali Khan, premiered in mid-January and immediately prompted\u00a0<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">controversy and criminal complaints. Things have escalated in recent weeks as several high-profile executives of Amazon Prime Video have been questioned by the authority.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Amazon Prime Video has been made to apologise. Sickening. <br \/>If you\u2019re offended by something, stop watching. Don\u2019t demand that it be scrubbed from existence. <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/hakPc1xqZ4\">pic.twitter.com\/hakPc1xqZ4<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Raja Sen (@RajaSen) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/RajaSen\/status\/1366762099863547904?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 2, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Prime Video has amassed millions of subscribers in India, where it competes with Disney&#8217;s Hotstar, Netflix, Times Internet&#8217;s MX Player, and dozens more streaming services. Amazon has grown more aggressive with Prime Video in India in recent months. It recently\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/amazon-launches-mobile-only-prime-video-subscription-in-india\/\">introduced an even cheaper subscription tier<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/scroll.in\/field\/978130\/cricket-amazon-prime-video-acquires-indian-territory-rights-for-all-matches-in-new-zealand\">secured rights<\/a> for streaming some cricket matches.<\/p>\n<p>Amazon\u2019s rare apology today comes days after New Delhi announced <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/25\/india-announces-sweeping-guidelines-for-social-media-on-demand-streaming-firms-and-digital-news-outlets\/\">new rules for on-demand video streaming services and social media firms<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Until now Amazon Prime Video and other streaming services have operated in India without having to worry too much about the nature of their content. But that\u2019s changing, according to the new rules.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe category classification of a content will take into account the potentially offensive impact of a film on matters such as caste, race, gender, religion, disability or sexuality that may arise in a wide range of works, and the classification decision will take account of the strength or impact of their inclusion,\u201d the new rules state.<\/p>\n<p>As we <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/25\/india-plays-hardball-with-amazon\/\">wrote recently<\/a>, the controversy surrounding the political drama and the new rules from India for streaming services are only few of the challenges that Amazon is facing in India, where it has <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/14\/amazon-to-invest-1-billion-to-digitize-small-businesses-in-india\/\">committed to deploy over $6.5 billion<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Last month, an influential India trader group that represents tens of millions of brick-and-mortar retailers <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/17\/indian-trader-group-calls-for-ban-on-amazon-following-dodging-regulations-claims\/\">called New Delhi to ban Amazon in the country<\/a> after an <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/investigates\/special-report\/amazon-india-operation\/\">investigation by Reuters<\/a> claimed that the American e-commerce group had given preferential treatment to a small group of sellers in India, publicly misrepresented its ties with those sellers and used them to circumvent foreign investment rules in the country.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"fFxTlC5cJw\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/24\/police-case-filed-against-netflix-executives-in-india-over-a-suitable-boy-kissing-scene\/\">Police case filed against Netflix executives in India over &#8216;A Suitable Boy&#8217; Cribs","url":"\/shows\/tc-cribs","attr":"","target":"","classes":[""],"description":"","object_id":1605180,"object":"custom","type":"custom","type_label":"Custom Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2119947,"date":"2021-03-02T17:05:46","date_gmt":"2021-03-03T01:05:46","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119947"},"modified":"2021-03-02T17:06:32","modified_gmt":"2021-03-03T01:06:32","slug":"facebooks-oversight-board-already-a-bit-frustrated-and-it-hasnt-made-a-call-on-trump-ban-yet","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/facebooks-oversight-board-already-a-bit-frustrated-and-it-hasnt-made-a-call-on-trump-ban-yet\/","title":{"rendered":"Facebook&#8217;s Oversight Board already &#8216;a bit frustrated&#8217; &#8212; and it hasn&#8217;t made a call on Trump ban yet"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The Facebook Oversight Board (FOB) is already feeling frustrated by the binary choices it&#8217;s expected to make as it reviews Facebook&#8217;s content moderation decisions, according to one of its members who was giving evidence to a <a href=\"https:\/\/parliamentlive.tv\/event\/index\/0e460b4b-d83c-478c-ba8a-c2588adec3fa\">UK House of Lords committee<\/a> today which <span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">is running an <\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/committees.parliament.uk\/work\/745\/freedom-of-expression-online\/\">enquiry<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> into freedom of expression online.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p>The FOB is currently <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/29\/facebook-trump-oversight-board-public-comment\/\">considering<\/a> whether to overturn Facebook&#8217;s ban on former US president, Donald Trump. The tech giant banned Trump &#8220;indefinitely&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/07\/mark-zuckerberg-announces-trump-banned-from-facebook-and-instagram-for-at-least-the-next-two-weeks\/\">earlier this year<\/a> after his supporters stormed the US capital.<\/p>\n<p>The chaotic insurrection on January 6 led to a number of deaths and widespread condemnation of how mainstream tech platforms had stood back and allowed Trump to use their tools as megaphones to whip up division and hate rather than enforcing their rules in his case.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Yet, after finally banning Trump, Facebook almost immediately referred the case to it\u2019s self-appointed and self-styled Oversight Board for review \u2014 opening up the prospect that its Trump ban could be reversed in short order via an exceptional review process that Facebook has fashioned, funded and staffed.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Tc8CsI1avU\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/facebook-oversight-board-trump-facebook-suspension\/\">Facebook&#8217;s Oversight Board will review the decision to suspend Trump<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook&#8217;s Oversight Board will review the decision to suspend Trump&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/facebook-oversight-board-trump-facebook-suspension\/embed\/#?secret=Tc8CsI1avU\" data-secret=\"Tc8CsI1avU\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Alan Rusbridger, a former editor of the British newspaper The Guardian \u2014 and one of 20 FOB members selected as an initial cohort (the Board&#8217;s full headcount will be double that) \u2014 avoided making a direct reference to the Trump case today, given the review is ongoing, but he implied that the binary choices it has at its disposal at this early stage aren&#8217;t as nuanced as he&#8217;d like.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhat happens if \u2014 without commenting on any high profile current cases &#8212; you didn\u2019t want to ban somebody for life but you wanted to have a &#8216;sin bin&#8217; so that if they misbehaved you could chuck them back off again?&#8221; he said, suggesting he&#8217;d like to be able to issue a soccer-style &#8220;yellow card&#8221; instead.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI think the Board will want to expand in its scope. I think we\u2019re already a bit frustrated by just saying take it down or leave it up,&#8221; he went on. &#8220;What happens if you want to&#8230; make something less viral? What happens if you want to put an interstitial?<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;So I think all these things are things that the Board may ask Facebook for in time. But we have to get our feet under the table first \u2014 we can do what we want.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAt some point we\u2019re going to ask to see the algorithm, I feel sure \u2014 whatever that means,&#8221; Rusbridger also told the committee. &#8220;Whether we can understand it when we see it is a different matter.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>To many people, Facebook&#8217;s Trump ban is uncontroversial &#8212; given the risk of further violence posed by letting Trump continue to use its megaphone to foment insurrection. There are also clear and repeat breaches of Facebook&#8217;s community standards if you want to be a stickler for its rules.<\/p>\n<p>Among supporters of the ban is Facebook&#8217;s former chief security officer, Alex Stamos, who has since been working on wider trust and safety issues for online platforms via the Stanford Internet Observatory.<\/p>\n<p>Stamos was urging both Twitter and Facebook to cut Trump off before everything kicked off, writing in early January: &#8220;There are no legitimate equities left and labeling won&#8217;t do it.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">The last reason to keep Trump&#39;s account up was the possibility that he would try to put the genie back in the bottle but as many expected, that is impossible for him.<\/p>\n<p>There will always be the alt-sites and peer-to-peer, but at least the damage he does would be more contained.<\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Alex Stamos (@alexstamos) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/alexstamos\/status\/1346932574317264898?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">January 6, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>But in the wake of big tech moving <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/09\/the-deplatforming-of-a-president\/\">almost as a unit<\/a> to finally put Trump on mute, a number of world leaders and lawmakers were quick to express misgivings at the big tech power flex.<\/p>\n<p>Germany&#8217;s chancellor called Twitter&#8217;s ban on him &#8220;problematic&#8221;, saying it raised troubling questions about the power of the platforms to interfere with speech. While other lawmakers in Europe seized on the unilateral action &#8212; saying it underlined the need for <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/11\/europe-seizes-on-social-medias-purging-of-trump-to-bang-the-drum-for-regulation\/\">proper democratic regulation of tech giants<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The sight of the world&#8217;s most powerful social media platforms being able to mute a democratically elected president (even one as divisive and unpopular as Trump) made politicians of all stripes feel queasy.<\/p>\n<p>Facebook&#8217;s entirely predictable response was, of course, to outsource this two-sided conundrum to the FOB. After all, that was its whole plan for the Board. The Board would be there to deal with the most headachey and controversial content moderation stuff.<\/p>\n<p>And on that level Facebook&#8217;s Oversight Board is doing exactly the job Facebook intended for it.<\/p>\n<p>But it&#8217;s interesting that this unofficial &#8216;supreme court&#8217; is already feeling frustrated by the limited binary choices it&#8217;s asked them for. (Of, in the Trump case, either reversing the ban entirely or continuing it indefinitely.)<\/p>\n<p>The FOB&#8217;s unofficial message seems to be that the tools are simply far too blunt. Although Facebook has never said it will be bound by any wider policy suggestions the Board might make &#8212; only that it will abide by the specific individual review decisions. (Which is why a common critique of the Board is that it&#8217;s toothless where it matters.)<\/p>\n<p>How aggressive the Board will be in pushing Facebook to be less frustrating very much remains to be seen.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cNone of this is going to be solved quickly,\u201d Rusbridger went on to tell the committee in more general remarks on the challenges of moderating speech in the digital era. Getting to grips with the Internet&#8217;s publishing revolution could in fact, he implied, take the work of generations &#8212; making the customary reference the long tail of societal disruption that flowed from Gutenberg inventing the printing press.<\/p>\n<p>If Facebook was hoping the FOB would kick hard (and thorny-in-its-side) questions around content moderation into long and intellectual grasses it&#8217;s surely delighted with the level of beard stroking which Rusbridger&#8217;s evidence implies is now going on inside the Board. (If, possibly, slightly less enchanted by the prospect of its appointees asking it if they can poke around its algorithmic black boxes.)<\/p>\n<p>Kate Klonick, an assistant professor at St John&#8217;s University Law School, was also giving evidence to the committee &#8212; having written an article on the inner workings of the FOB, published recently in the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.newyorker.com\/tech\/annals-of-technology\/inside-the-making-of-facebooks-supreme-court\">New Yorker<\/a>, after she was given wide-ranging access by Facebook to observe the process of the body being set up.<\/p>\n<p>The Lords committee was keen to learn more on the workings of the FOB and pressed the witnesses several times on the question of the Board&#8217;s independence from Facebook.<\/p>\n<p>Rusbridger batted away concerns on that front \u2014 saying \u201cwe don\u2019t feel we work for Facebook at all\u201d. Though Board members are paid by Facebook via a trust it set up to put the FOB at arm&#8217;s length from the corporate mothership. And the committee didn&#8217;t shy away or raising the payment point to query how genuinely independent they can be?<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I feel highly independent,\u201d Rusbridger said. \u201cI don\u2019t think there\u2019s any obligation at all to be nice to Facebook or to be horrible to Facebook.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;One of the nice things about this Board is occasionally people will say but if we did that that will scupper Facebook\u2019s economic model in such and such a country. To which we answer well that\u2019s not our problem. Which is a very liberating thing,&#8221; he added.<\/p>\n<p>Of course it\u2019s hard to imagine a sitting member of the FOB being able to answer the independence question any other way \u2014 unless they were simultaneously resigning their commission (which, to be clear, Rusbridger wasn\u2019t).<\/p>\n<p>He confirmed that Board members can serve three terms of three years apiece &#8212; so he could have almost a decade of beard-stroking on Facebook&#8217;s behalf ahead of him.<\/p>\n<p>Klonick, meanwhile, emphasized the scale of the challenge it had been for Facebook to try to build from scratch a quasi-independent oversight body and create distance between itself and its claimed watchdog.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cBuilding an institution to be a watchdog institution \u2014 it is incredibly hard to transition to institution-building and to break those bonds [between the Board and Facebook] and set up these new people with frankly this huge set of problems and a new technology and a new back end and a content management system and everything,&#8221; she said.<\/p>\n<p>Rusbridger had said the Board went through an extensive training process which involved participation from Facebook representatives during the &#8216;onboarding&#8217;. But went on to describe a moment when the training had finished and the FOB realized some Facebook reps were still joining their calls &#8212; saying that at that point the Board felt empowered to tell Facebook to leave.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThis was exactly the type of moment \u2014 having watched this \u2014 that I knew had to happen,\u201d added Klonick. \u201cThere had to be some type of formal break \u2014 and it was told to me that this was a natural moment that they had done their training and this was going to be moment of push back and breaking away from the nest. And this was it.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>However if your measure of independence is not having Facebook <em>literally listening in on<\/em> <em>the Board&#8217;s calls<\/em> you do have to query how much Kool Aid Facebook may have successfully doled out to its chosen and willing participants over the long and intricate process of programming its own watchdog &#8212; including to extra outsiders it allowed in to observe the set up.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Dipeq76Iv8\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/28\/under-consideration\/\">Toothless: Facebook proposes a weak Oversight Board<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Toothless: Facebook proposes a weak Oversight Board&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/28\/under-consideration\/embed\/#?secret=Dipeq76Iv8\" data-secret=\"Dipeq76Iv8\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The committee was also interested in the fact the FOB has so far mostly ordered Facebook to reinstate content its moderators had previously taken down.<\/p>\n<p>In <a href=\"https:\/\/uk.news.yahoo.com\/facebooks-oversight-body-overturns-four-154522911.html\">January<\/a>, when the Board issued its first decisions, it overturned four out of five Facebook takedowns &#8212; including in relation to a number of hate speech cases. The move quickly attracted criticism over the direction of travel. After all, the wider critique of Facebook&#8217;s business is it&#8217;s far too reluctant to remove toxic content (it only <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/12\/facebook-in-a-reversal-will-now-ban-holocaust-denial-content-under-its-hate-speech-policy\/\">banned holocaust denial last year<\/a>, for example). And lo! Here&#8217;s its self-styled &#8216;Oversight Board&#8217; taking decisions to <em>reverse<\/em>\u00a0hate speech takedowns&#8230;<\/p>\n<p>The unofficial and oppositional &#8216;Real Facebook Board&#8217; &#8212; which is truly independent and heavily critical of Facebook &#8212; pounced and decried the decisions as &#8220;shocking&#8221;, saying the FOB had &#8220;bent over backwards to excuse hate&#8221;.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">\ud83d\udcddSTATEMENT\ud83d\udcdd &#8211; January 28, 2020<\/p>\n<p>Real Facebook Oversight Board Responds to Facebook <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/OversightBoard?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@OversightBoard<\/a> Rulings &#8211; \u201cBent Over Backward to Excuse Hate;\u201d \u201cShocking;\u201d \u201cSelf-Congratulatory\u201d<\/p>\n<p>cc: <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/MuslimAdvocates?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@MuslimAdvocates<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Avaaz?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@Avaaz<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/ColorOfChange?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@ColorOfChange<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/freepress?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@freepress<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/sY1c0D4r3F\">pic.twitter.com\/sY1c0D4r3F<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; The Real Facebook Oversight Board (@FBoversight) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/FBoversight\/status\/1354813107164463113?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">January 28, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Klonick said the reality is that the FOB is not Facebook&#8217;s supreme court &#8212; but rather it&#8217;s essentially just &#8220;a dispute resolution mechanism for users&#8221;.<\/p>\n<p>If that assessment is true &#8212; and it sounds spot on, so long as you recall the fantastically tiny number of users who get to use it &#8212; the amount of PR Facebook has been able to generate off of something that should really just be a standard feature of its platform is truly incredible.<\/p>\n<p>Klonick argued that the Board&#8217;s early reversals were the result of it hearing from users objecting to content takedowns &#8212; which had made it &#8220;sympathetic&#8221; to their complaints.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Absolute frustration at not knowing specifically what rule was broken or how to avoid breaking the rule again or what they did to be able to get there or to be able to tell their side of the story,&#8221; she said, listing the kinds of things Board members had told her they were hearing from users who had petitioned for a review of a takedown decision against them.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I think that what you&#8217;re seeing in the Board&#8217;s decision is, first and foremost, to try to build some of that back in,&#8221; she suggested. &#8220;Is that the signal that they&#8217;re sending back to Facebook &#8212; that&#8217;s it&#8217;s pretty low hanging fruit to be honest. Which is let people know the exact rule, given them a fact to fact type of analysis or application of the rule to the facts and give them that kind of read in to what they&#8217;re seeing and people will be happier with what&#8217;s going on.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Or at least just feel a little bit more like there is a process and it&#8217;s not just this black box that&#8217;s censoring them.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In his response to the committee&#8217;s query, Rusbridger discussed how he approaches review decision-making.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIn most judgements I begin by thinking well why would we restrict freedom of speech in this particular case \u2014 and that does get you into interesting questions,\u201d he said, having earlier summed up his school of thought on speech as akin to the \u2018fight bad speech with more speech\u2019 Justice Brandeis type view.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe right not to be offended has been engaged by one of the cases \u2014 as opposed to the borderline between being offended and being harmed,&#8221; he went on. \u201cThat issue has been argued about by political philosophers for a long time and it certainly will never be settled absolutely.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;But if you went along with establishing a right not to be offended that would have huge implications for the ability to discuss almost anything in the end. And yet there have been one or two cases where essentially Facebook, in taking something down, has invoked something like that.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cHarm as oppose to offence is clearly something you would treat differently,\u201d he added. \u201cAnd we\u2019re in the fortunate position of being able to hire in experts and seek advisors on the harm here.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>While Rusbridger didn&#8217;t sound troubled about the challenges and pitfalls facing the Board when it may have to set the &#8220;borderline&#8221; between offensive speech and harmful speech itself &#8212; being able to (further) outsource expertise presumably helps &#8212; he did raise a number of other operational concerns during the session. Including over the lack of technical expertise among current board members (who were purely Facebook&#8217;s picks).<\/p>\n<p>Without technical expertise how can the Board \u2018examine the algorithm\u2019, as he suggested it would want to, because it won&#8217;t be able to understand Facebook\u2019s content distribution machine in any meaningful way?<\/p>\n<p>Since the Board currently lacks technical expertise, it does raise wider questions about its function &#8212; and whether its first learned cohort might not be played as useful idiots from Facebook&#8217;s self-interested perspective &#8212; by helping it gloss over and deflect deeper scrutiny of its algorithmic, money-minting choices.<\/p>\n<p>If you don&#8217;t really understand how the Facebook machine functions, technically and economically, how can you conduct any kind of meaningful oversight at all? (Rusbridger evidently gets that &#8212; but is also content to wait and see how the process plays out. No doubt the intellectual exercise and insider view is fascinating. &#8220;So far I&#8217;m finding it highly absorbing,&#8221; as he admitted in his evidence opener.)<\/p>\n<p>\u201cPeople say to me you\u2019re on that Board but it\u2019s well known that the algorithms reward emotional content that polarises communities because that makes it more addictive. Well I don\u2019t know if that\u2019s true or not \u2014 and I think as a board we\u2019re going to have to get to grips with that,&#8221; he went on to say. &#8220;Even if that takes many sessions with coders speaking very slowly so that we can understand what they\u2019re saying.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI do think our responsibility will be to understand what these machines are \u2014 the machines that are going in rather than the machines that are moderating,\u201d he added. \u201cWhat their metrics are.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Both witnesses raised another concern: That the kind of complex, nuanced moderation decisions the Board is making won\u2019t be able to scale &#8212; suggesting they\u2019re too specific to be able to generally inform AI-based moderation. Nor will they necessarily be able to be acted on by the staffed moderation system that Facebook currently operates (which gives its thousand of human moderators a fantastically tiny amount of thinking time per content decision).<\/p>\n<p>Despite that the issue of Facebook&#8217;s vast scale vs the Board&#8217;s limited and Facebook-defined function &#8212; to fiddle at the margins of its content empire &#8212; was one overarching point that hung uneasily over the session, without being properly grappled with.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI think your question about &#8216;is this easily communicated&#8217; is a really good one that we\u2019re wrestling with a bit,\u201d Rusbridger said, conceding that he\u2019d had to brain up on a whole bunch of unfamiliar \u201chuman rights protocols and norms from around the world\u201d to feel qualified to rise to the demands of the review job.<\/p>\n<p>Scaling that level of training to the tens of thousands of moderators Facebook currently employs to carry out content moderation would of course be eye-wateringly expensive. Nor is it on offer from Facebook. Instead it&#8217;s hand-picked a crack team of 40 very expensive and learned experts to tackle an infinitesimally smaller number of content decisions.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI think it\u2019s important that the decisions we come to are understandable by human moderators,&#8221; Rusbridger added. &#8220;Ideally they\u2019re understandable by machines as well \u2014 and there is a tension there because sometimes you look at the facts of a case and you decide it in a particular way with reference to those three standards [Facebook\u2019s community standard, Facebook\u2019s values and \u201ca human rights filter\u201d]. But in the knowledge that that\u2019s going to be quite a tall order for a machine to understand the nuance between that case and another case.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cBut, you know, these are early days.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cl2XzAwHOw\"><p><a Speech","slug":"free-speech","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/39274"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=39274"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=39274"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=39274"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=39274"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2119979,"date":"2021-03-02T17:03:06","date_gmt":"2021-03-03T01:03:06","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119979"},"modified":"2021-03-02T17:07:52","modified_gmt":"2021-03-03T01:07:52","slug":"atomic-which-only-funds-the-startups-it-launches-just-closed-its-newest-fund-with-260-million","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/atomic-which-only-funds-the-startups-it-launches-just-closed-its-newest-fund-with-260-million\/","title":{"rendered":"Atomic, which only funds the startups it launches, just closed its newest fund with $260 million"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Jack Abraham has a lot of confidence in what he&#8217;s building. Then again, you can&#8217;t be immodest or unsure of yourself if you&#8217;re going to bet exclusively on your own startups as an investor, which is precisely the model that Abraham&#8217;s San Francisco-based venture studio, <a href=\"https:\/\/atomic.vc\/\">Atomic<strong>,<\/strong><\/a> has followed since it was launched nine years ago.<\/p>\n<p>It all started with $10 million of Abraham&#8217;s own money, capital he amassed by selling his first startup, a local shopping engine called Milo, to eBay in 2010, for $75 million. Abraham had dropped out of Wharton as an undergrad with $500,000 from a professor who believed that Abraham &#8212; whose father founded ComScore &#8212; would himself be a company-building machine.<\/p>\n<p>The professor had good instincts. After selling Milo at age 24, Abraham spent more than three years building products inside of eBay and learning how to lead multiple teams before beginning to look outward, making angel bets, including on Uber and Pinterest, and, he says, spreading around some of his ideas. (Among these, he says, he &#8220;invented Postmates. I gave the founders literally the idea for the company; they were working on a B2B company at the time. I was fairly early on there; that helped spawn the whole food delivery thing.&#8221;)<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>He had so many ideas &#8212; hundreds, he says &#8212; that not long afterward, he created Atomic with cofounder Andrew Dudum, a Wharton peer who is also the son of entrepreneurs and who also <a href=\"https:\/\/thesign.al\/andrew-dudum-cofounder-partner-at-atomic-2\/\">dropped out of college<\/a> to join the startup world. (Dudum&#8217;s first stop was a then-nascent <a href=\"https:\/\/en.wikipedia.org\/wiki\/TokBox\">startup<\/a> backed by Sequoia Capital.)<\/p>\n<p>At first, Atomic worked on one company. The following year, it worked on two. By 2018, the outfit had built out a team that could handle many of the back-end functions that startups need to thrive, from recruiting to accounting, and launched 10 companies. Impressed investors gave the firm $150 million to create even more startups.<\/p>\n<p>By then, Abraham and Dudum had brought in two other general partners: Chester Ng and Andrew Salamon. Salamon left in 2019 to launch his own venture studio, <a href=\"https:\/\/materialcompanies.com\/#team\">Material<\/a>, with Blue Apron founder Matt Salzberg. The same year, JD Ross, one of a handful of cofounders of the <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/opendoor-closes-at-31-25-on-first-day-of-trading\/\">newly public<\/a> company Opendoor, joined Atomic as a general partner.<\/p>\n<p>The firm has only picked up speed since. Indeed, at this point, Atomic has created &#8220;dozens&#8221; of startups &#8212; including roughly one per month last year, says Abraham. It also just closed on $260 million in new capital commitments, including from a prominent university that now serves as its anchor investor but would prefer not to be named publicly.<\/p>\n<p>Citing &#8220;proprietary aspects&#8221; to the model, Abraham declines to explain how Atomic&#8217;s economics work, except to acknowledge that it operates in &#8220;more of a fund context instead of a holding company&#8221; where investors would essentially be buying stakes in Atomic itself.<\/p>\n<p>Certainly, it&#8217;s easy to appreciate the enthusiasm of Atomic&#8217;s investors, including early backers like Peter Thiel and Marc Andreessen. Abraham and Dudum are both compelling storytellers, as we&#8217;ve witnessed first-hand in interviewing them at different times. The firm is also starting to see some exits.<\/p>\n<p>One of Atomic&#8217;s creations, the telehealth company Hims, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/telehealth-startup-hims-fell-in-its-public-trading-debut-and-thats-fine-with-its-ceo\/\">taken public<\/a> in January through a blank-check company in a deal that valued the company at $1.6 billion, and its shares have been rising since. As of this writing, the three-and-a-half-year-old outfit &#8212; run by Dudum, who is doing double-duty as Hims&#8217;s CEO and a general partner with Atomic &#8212; boasts a market cap of $2.9 billion.<\/p>\n<p>Atomic also sold a voice-powered sales startup, TalkIQ, to the company Dialpad in 2018 for what Forbes reported at the time to be a &#8220;<a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/alexkonrad\/2018\/05\/16\/dialpad-buys-talkiq\/?sh=4595ec8387d0\">little under $50 million<\/a>.&#8221; TalkIQ had raised $22 million altogether.<\/p>\n<p>More exits are coming, suggests Abraham. &#8220;There many companies we have that are now approaching the sort of growth and run rate where they have the ability to go public, even as soon as in the next year,&#8221; he says.<\/p>\n<p>One of those eventual prospects is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.replicant.ai\/\">Replicant<\/a>, an autonomous call center startup that has raised $35 million since its 2017 founding, including a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/kenrickcai\/2020\/09\/10\/replicant-series-a-call-center-voice-ai\/?sh=2b040a9d4266\">$27 million Series A round<\/a> led by Norwest Venture Partners back in September. Another Atomic startup, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.homebound.com\/\">Homebound<\/a>, a three-year-old home-building outfit that handles everything from financing to construction, has also enjoyed <a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/samanthasharf\/2020\/01\/16\/she-almost-lost-her-home-in-californias-wildfires-instead-she-built-a-200-million-business\">some momentum<\/a>, as well as attracted $53 million from investors.<\/p>\n<p>Though Atomic prides itself on &#8220;pressure testing&#8221; its ideas, not every startup has been a hit. A photo-sharing app called Ever was quickly shut down after <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nbcnews.com\/tech\/security\/millions-people-uploaded-photos-ever-app-then-company-used-them-n1003371\">NBC reported<\/a> that the photos people shared were used to train the company\u2019s facial recognition system. A sleep-tracking specialist, Rested, was also shut down.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, ZenReach, a Wi-Fi marketing company that had collected at least <a href=\"https:\/\/www.crunchbase.com\/organization\/zenreach\">$94 million<\/a> from investors through 2018, laid off<a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/zenreach-lays-off-20-of-staff-following-co-founders-departure-1519952702\"> 20%<\/a> of its employees that same year. A CEO who&#8217;d been brought aboard by Abraham and who was previously an operating partner with Atomic, has since moved on to a role elsewhere.<\/p>\n<p>If not all of its ideas set the world on fire, Atomic has no shortage of others.<\/p>\n<p>Asked about some of the areas where he sees the most opportunity to innovate, Abraham quickly ticks off &#8220;healthcare, finance, education, real estate, and other large industries where truthfully, when you&#8217;re inside them, you understand how broken they are, and they are broken up and down the entire stack.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;You study them,&#8221; he says, &#8220;and then you wonder how is this possible this happened.&#8221;<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Jack Abraham has a lot of confidence in what he&#8217;s building. Then again, you can&#8217;t be immodest or unsure of yourself if you&#8217;re going to bet exclusively on your own startups as an investor, which is precisely the model that Abraham&#8217;s San Francisco-based venture studio, Atomic, has followed since it was launched nine years ago. Capital India\u2019s Surge invests $2M in sales engagement platform Outplay"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><div id=\"attachment_2119464\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplayers-team-pic.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119464\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Outplay&#8217;s team members on a video call<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Sales engagement platforms (SEP) help sales teams automate and track the large number of tasks they need to do each day as they contact leads and hone in on potential deals. Focused on small-to-medium-sized companies, SEP startup <a href=\"https:\/\/outplayhq.com\/\">Outplay<\/a> announced today it has raised $2 million from Sequoia Capital India&#8217;s Surge program for early-stage startups.<\/p>\n<p>Outplay was founded in January 2020 by brothers Ram and Laxman Papineni and now counts more than 300 clients. Before launching Outplay, the Papineni brothers <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/01\/12\/appvirality\/\">built AppVirality<\/a>, a referall marketing tool for app developers.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Laxman told TechCrunch that Outplay&#8217;s customers come from sectors like IT, computer software, marketing and advertising and recruiting, and most are based in North America and Europe.<\/p>\n<p>Outplay is designed for teams that use multiple channels to reach potential customers, including phone calls, text messages, email, live chats on websites, and social media platforms like LinkedIn or Twitter. It integrates with customer relationship management platforms like Salesforce and Pipedrive, giving sales people a new interface that includes productivity and automation tools to cut the time they spend on administrative tasks.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119465\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119465\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2119465\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg\" alt=\"Screenshots of Outplay's sales engagement platform for automating sales tasks\" width=\"1024\" height=\"640\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg 2880w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=150,94 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=300,188 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=768,480 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=680,425 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=1536,960 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=2048,1280 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Outplay-platform.jpg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119465\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Outplay&#8217;s platform<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>For example, Outplay can be used create sequences that send initial messages through different platforms, and then automatically follows up with new messages if there isn&#8217;t a reply within a pre-set time frame. Outplay also provides analytics to help sales people track how well sales campaigns are working.<\/p>\n<p>Two of Outplay&#8217;s biggest competitors are Outreach and SalesLoft, both of which hit unicorn status in recent funding rounds. Laxman said Outplay is focused on ease of use, with other differentiators including more integrations with CRMs and other software, and a strong customer support team.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"RxiJ8nRAiG\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/16\/outreach-nabs-50m-at-a-1-33b-valuation-for-its-sales-engagement-tools\/\">Outreach nabs $50M at a $1.33B valuation for software that helps with sales engagement<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; }],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576859879"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576859879"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576859879"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576859879"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576859880,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/sales-engagement-platform\/","name":"sales platform","slug":"sales-engagement-platform","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576859880"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576859880"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576859880"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576859880"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576859880"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2119149,"date":"2021-03-02T15:39:25","date_gmt":"2021-03-02T23:39:25","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119149"},"modified":"2021-03-02T15:39:25","modified_gmt":"2021-03-02T23:39:25","slug":"facebook-can-save-itself-by-becoming-a-b-corporation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/facebook-can-save-itself-by-becoming-a-b-corporation\/","title":{"rendered":"Facebook can save itself by becoming a B Corporation"},"content":{"rendered":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Ann Florini<\/span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor<\/span>\n\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/ann-florini-5a25a327\">Ann Florini<\/a> is Clinical Professor at Thunderbird School of Global Management at the Arizona State University.\t<\/div>\n\t\n\t<\/div>\n\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Brett Hurt<\/span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor<\/span>\n\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"contributor__twitter\">\n\t\t\t<a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/databrett\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<svg class=\"icon icon--twitter icon--white\" viewBox=\"0 0 20 20\" version=\"1.1\" aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter<\/title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"\/>\t<\/svg>\n\t\t\t\t<\/a>\n\t\t<\/div>\n\t\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tBrett Hurt is CEO and co-founder of <a href=\"https:\/\/data.world\/\">Data.World<\/a>.\t<\/div>\n\t\n\t<\/div>\n<\/div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">As Facebook confronts outrage among its employees and the public for mishandling multiple decisions about its role in shaping public discourse, it is becoming clear that it cannot solve its conundrums without a major change in its business model. And a new model is readily available: for-benefit status.<\/p>\n<p>For decades, a misguided ideology has warped companies, economies and societies: that the sole purpose of corporations is to maximize short-term returns to one set of stakeholders &#8212; those who have bought shares. Neither law nor history requires this to be true.<\/p>\n<p>But shareholder value-maximization ideology has become cemented in far too much corporate practice at the expense of societal well-being. This is manifested in many ways: a slavish adherence to the judgment of the &#8220;market,&#8221; even when other social signals are more powerful; executives enriched by stock options; companies fearful of \u201cactivist investors\u201d who attack whenever stock prices fail to meet quarterly \u201cexpectations\u201d and often-frivolous shareholder lawsuits pushing for stock gains at all costs.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The pandemic, however, has accelerated an already-spreading recognition that shareholder value maximization is often a harmful choice &#8212; not by any means a moral imperative or even a fiduciary responsibility.<\/p>\n<p>Major institutions of capitalism are converging on a new vision for it. The 2019\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/opportunity.businessroundtable.org\/ourcommitment\/\">Business Roundtable CEO statement<\/a>\u00a0said that corporate strategy should benefit\u00a0<i>all<\/i> stakeholders \u2013 including shareholders, yes, but equally customers, employees, suppliers, and the communities in which companies operate. BlackRock CEO Larry Fink\u2019s recent annual letters assert new views of how that investment company, the world\u2019s largest, should invest the trillions it oversees.<\/p>\n<p>Fink\u2019s 2019 letter spelled out a\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.blackrock.com\/americas-offshore\/2019-larry-fink-ceo-letter\">new vision for corporate purpose<\/a>; the subsequent 2020 and 2021 letters focused on business\u2019 responsibility around climate change, particularly in light of the pandemic. The <a href=\"https:\/\/bcorporation.net\/\">B Corporation<\/a>\u00a0and conscious capitalism movements are growing. The World Economic Forum is championing a \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/www.fourthsector.org\/fsdi\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fourth Sector<\/a>,\u201d combining purpose with profit. Business schools, facing student rebellions against a purely profit-maximizing curriculum, are rapidly changing what they teach.<\/p>\n<p>And with society under siege, many more businesses, including social media, are scrambling to seem like good corporate citizens. They have no choice.<\/p>\n<p>Facebook, for example, has doubled down on philanthropy and new efforts to combat misinformation, even as usage and share price soar. Platforms like WhatsApp (owned by Facebook) have become essential services to connect people whose physical ties have been abruptly severed during the global pandemic. Shelter-in-place has become, in many ways, shelter-in-Facebook-properties.<\/p>\n<p>But Facebook and its brethren remain fragile. Since the 2016 presidential election in the U.S., Facebook has faced governmental hearings and regulation, public uproar (#deleteFacebook), and huge fines for invading privacy and undermining democracy. These calls were amplified in the weeks following the January 6 Capitol riot. Separately, it faces allegations of bias, largely (though not entirely) from the political right. These have led to calls for the revocation or reform of Section 230 of the Communications Decency Act, which grants it immunity from the actions of its users.<\/p>\n<p>A giant company that is simultaneously essential and pilloried is vulnerable. Just ask the ghosts of John D. Rockefeller and his fellow robber barons, whose huge monopolies industrialized America more than 100 years ago. Journalistic muckrakers and public outrage targeted them for their abusive practices until the government finally broke up their companies via antitrust legislation.<\/p>\n<p>Because Mark Zuckerberg maintains complete majority control of Facebook, he could unilaterally quell public opprobrium and fend off heavy-handed regulation singlehandedly by transforming Facebook into a new kind of business: a for-benefit corporation.<\/p>\n<p>Under the\u00a0<a href=\"&quot;https:\/\/benefitcorp.net\/businesses?\">Public Benefit Corporation<\/a> legal model, firms bind themselves to a public benefit mission statement and carry out required ongoing reporting on both the standard financials\u00a0<i>and<\/i>\u00a0on how the company is living up to its mission. That status protects the company against profit-demanding shareholder lawsuits, and also attracts employees and investors who want to combine profit with purpose.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"http:\/\/data.world\/\">Data.world<\/a> is one of the thousands of certified B Corporations that have seen good returns on financial metrics.\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.allbirds.com\/\">Allbirds<\/a>, for example, launched in a few sustainable materials using a pro-sustainability process to manufacture comfortable shoes, quickly reaching revenues of $100 million and valuation of $1.7 billion in an industry fraught with sustainability and human rights concerns. Other household names that are B Corps include <a href=\"https:\/\/www.thebodyshop.com\/en-us\/\">The Body Shop<\/a>,\u00a0<a href=\"&quot;https:\/\/www.coursera.org\/\">Coursera<\/a>,\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.danone.com\/\">Danone<\/a>, the\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.jamieoliver.com\/\">Jamie Oliver Group<\/a>,\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.kingarthurbaking.com\/\">King Arthur Flour<\/a>,\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/numitea.com\/\">Numi Tea<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.patagonia.com\/home\/\">Patagonia<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Many companies that have not undergone formal B Certification from B Labs have nonetheless done well while transforming their business practices, such as the carpet and flooring company\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.interface.com\/\">Interface<\/a>. Some firms incorporate ESG principles into their management systems \u2013 the $24 billion (market cap) Dutch life sciences company\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.dsm.com\/corporate\/home.html\">DSM<\/a> has for years had meaningful sustainability targets for its senior management that account for fully 50 percent of their annual bonuses. Both Interface and DSM attribute much of their commercial success to their attention to non-financial considerations.<\/p>\n<p>A for-benefit Facebook could similarly relate to the world differently, avoiding many of the reputational shocks and regulatory responses that have led to huge stock dips and enormous fines. Its operations would align with Zuckerberg\u2019s proclaimed purpose to enable the potential abundance that results from connecting everyone in the world.<\/p>\n<p>Imagine a Facebook town hall as a true public square, not just another way to gather and sell people\u2019s data without their explicit consent. Imagine a Facebook that put its users first and its advertisers second; that revealed where ads came from; that\u00a0<i>earned<\/i>\u00a0your attention in a way that you controlled rather than through machine-driven algorithms maximizing your attention for good or ill. Such a for-benefit Facebook could create true buy-in and transparency with its massive community around the world.<\/p>\n<p>Of course, such steps as Facebook\u2019s new\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/about.fb.com\/news\/2020\/05\/welcoming-the-oversight-board\/\">Oversight Board<\/a>, which may provide some meaningful review, don\u2019t require a legal change. But if shareholders and employees continue to be rewarded primarily by the success of the problematic ad revenue model, a continuing conflict between private gain and public benefit makes it impossible to have confidence about what is happening behind the scenes. A shift to for-benefit incorporation and appropriate certification brings with it different performance metrics and accountability systems with <a href=\"https:\/\/bcorporation.net\/directory\/dataworld-inc\">public scores<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>In changing Facebook into a for-benefit corporation, Zuckerberg could insulate himself against presidential rage while rehabilitating his reputation \u2014 and his company&#8217;s. It would likely create vast ripples both in Silicon Valley and beyond \u2014 and it might help transform capitalism itself.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>In changing Facebook Apache Cassandra<\/a>; announcing <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/microsoft-launches-azure-percept-its-new-hardware-and-software-platform-to-bring-ai-to-the-edge\/\">a hardware and
