runch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/449557102"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=449557102"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=449557102"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=449557102"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557028,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/mobile\/","name":"Mobile","slug":"mobile","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/449557028"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=449557028"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=449557028"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=449557028"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2119888,"date":"2021-03-02T12:55:38","date_gmt":"2021-03-02T20:55:38","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119888"},"modified":"2021-03-02T13:03:51","modified_gmt":"2021-03-02T21:03:51","slug":"spinezone-is-the-latest-health-tech-startup-to-raise-millions-in-the-musculoskeletal-space","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/spinezone-is-the-latest-health-tech-startup-to-raise-millions-in-the-musculoskeletal-space\/","title":{"rendered":"SpineZone is the latest health tech startup to raise millions in the musculoskeletal space"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">SpineZone is a startup that creates personalized exercise programs and treatment for neck and back pain. The company uses an online platform and in-person clinics to deliver a curriculum that, ideally, helps patients avoid the need for prescription drugs, injections and surgeries, and providers then avoid the cost of all of the above. Co-founded by brothers Kian Raiszadeh and Kamshad Raiszadeh, the company tells TechCrunch that it has raised $12 million in a Series A round led by Polaris Partners and Providence Ventures, with participation from Martin Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>At its core, SpineZone is a virtual physical therapy platform augmented by in-person clinics. The latter bit is important because it takes a video repository, which has health outcomes baked into it, and helps get those same users some real-life support.<\/p>\n<p>Patients can log onto the site, either through smartphone or laptop, and then answer a series of questions around pain and risk factors. Then, patients can go through a series of exercises. These exercises are created in tandem with professionals, and are based on peer-reviewed and evidence-based articles on musculoskeletal health.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Beyond this digital archive of videos, SpineZone offers an in-person clinic option to help patients practice these exercises. Off of this strategy, the startup claims that it has \u201c1 million lives under management.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>SpineZone\u2019s value proposition is that it helps payers and providers, whether that be employers, clinics or health plans such as Cigna or Aetna, avoid placing their patients in surgeries, which are expensive. By taking care of pain issues before they bubble up, SpineZone says that its current partners have been able to have a 50% reduction in surgery rate (it\u2019s worth noting that COVID-19 could also play a role in this because it is high-risk to enter a medical facility).<\/p>\n<p>Partners are happy because footing the bill of a non-operative procedure is remarkably cheaper than a non-operative procedure.<\/p>\n<p>The cost saving that a medical center could endure can be in the millions. For example, the Sharp Community Medical Group saved $3.4 million in cost savings after working with SpineZone for two years.<\/p>\n<p>SpineZone\u2019s business model is a smidge more complicated than your classic SaaS fee. For example, it charges a clinic based on the number of members it serves per month, and also shares in the downside. For example, if SpineZone promises to get a clinic to $12 million in spend from $15 million, and the cost ends up being $17 million, the company will pay the clinic a portion of the difference. Alternatively, if SpineZone got the clinic to $10 million, even below estimates, it shares in the upside.<\/p>\n<p>SpineZone joins a cohort of health tech startups that focus on musculoskeletal conditions. Venture-backed competitors include Peerwell, Force Therapeutics and Hinge Health, which <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/05\/hinge-healthy-d\/\">was most recently valued at $3 billion, with plans to go public.<\/a><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ECjZ5wHyTY\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/05\/hinge-healthy-d\/\">Sources: Hinge Health has raised $300M Series D at a $3B valuation<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Sources: Hinge Health has raised $300M Series D at a $3B valuation&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/05\/hinge-healthy-d\/embed\/#?secret=ECjZ5wHyTY\" data-secret=\"ECjZ5wHyTY\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>In order to win, many startups, SpineZone including, need value-based care to replace fee-for-service care. Value-based care is the idea that doctors are paid for outcomes instead of the number of times you enter a doctor\u2019s office. The end goal is that this format creates monetary incentives around getting to an outcome faster: If a doctor is going to make $30,000 on fixing a knee, regardless of whether it takes two appointments or 20 appointments, they might as well do a more thorough job upon check-up instead of elongating the process. The flipside of this, of course, is that doctors might optimize for outcome volume and speed rather than the quality of the result itself.<\/p>\n<p>While SpineZone\u2019s early traction is promising, the healthcare ecosystem still has a ways to go before value-based models take precedence. Right now, Kian\u00a0Raiszadeh estimates that 10 to 20% of revenue in a medical center comes from value-based care. SpineZone is projecting that it will get to 50% of revenue in the near future.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cAnd that\u2019s the biggest evolution and tallest lift that we\u2019re expecting,\u201d he said.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CEShiMR8yi\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/8-vcs-agree-behavioral-support-and-remote-visits-make-digital-health-a-strong-bet-for-2021\/\">8 VCs agree: Behavioral support and remote visits make digital health a strong bet for 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;8 VCs agree: Behavioral support and remote visits make digital health a strong bet for 2021&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/8-vcs-agree-behavioral-support-and-remote-visits-make-digital-health-a-strong-bet-for-2021\/embed\/#?secret=CEShiMR8yi\" data-secret=\"CEShiMR8yi\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premiere \u2018how-to\u2019 event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. You\u2019ll hear first-hand how some of the most successful founders and VCs build their businesses, raise money and manage their portfolios. We\u2019ll cover every aspect of company-building: Fundraising, recruiting, sales, legal, PR, marketing and brand building. Each session also has audience participation built-in \u2013 there\u2019s ample time included in each for audience questions and discussion.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>\t<iframe\n\t\t\tid=\"wpcom-iframe-dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\twidth=\"99%\"\n\t\t\theight=\"1500\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https:\/\/tcprotectedembed.com\/protected-iframe\/dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\tscrolling=\"true\"\n\t\t\tframeborder=\"0\"\n\t\t\tclass=\"wpcom-protected-iframe\"\n\t>\n\t<\/iframe>\n\t<script says China-backed hackers are exploiting Exchange zero-days"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Microsoft is warning customers that a new China state-sponsored threat actor is exploiting four previously undisclosed security flaws in Exchange Server, an enterprise email product built by the software giant.<\/p>\n<p>The technology company said Tuesday that it believes the hacking group, which it calls Hafnium, tries to steal information from a broad range of U.S.-based organizations, including law firms and defense contractors, but also infectious disease researchers and policy think tanks.<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft said Hafnium used the four newly discovered security vulnerabilities to break into Exchange email servers running on company networks, granting the attackers to steal data from a victim&#8217;s organization \u2014 such as email accounts and address books \u2014 and the ability to plant malware. When used together, the four vulnerabilities create an attack chain that can compromise vulnerable on-premise servers running Exchange 2013 and later.<\/p>\n<p>Hafnium operates out of China, but uses servers located in the U.S. to launch its attacks, the company said. Microsoft said that Hafnium was the primary threat group it detected using these four new vulnerabilities. <em>(An earlier version of Microsoft&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/on-the-issues\/2021\/03\/02\/new-nation-state-cyberattacks\/\">blog post<\/a> incorrectly said Hafnium was the &#8220;only&#8221; group to exploit the vulnerabilities.)<\/em><\/p>\n<p>Microsoft declined to say how many successful attacks it had seen, but described the number as &#8220;limited.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Patches to fix those four security vulnerabilities are now out, a week earlier than the company&#8217;s typical patching schedule, usually reserved for the second Tuesday in each month.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Even though we\u2019ve worked quickly to deploy an update for the Hafnium exploits, we know that many nation-state actors and criminal groups will move quickly to take advantage of any unpatched systems,&#8221; said Tom Burt, Microsoft\u2019s vice president for customer security.<\/p>\n<p>The company said it has also briefed U.S. government agencies on its findings, but that the Hafnium attacks are not related to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/17\/fireeye-breach-solarwinds-federal-agencies\/\">the SolarWinds-related espionage campaign<\/a> against U.S. federal agencies. In the last days of the Trump administration, the National Security Agency and the FBI said that <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/05\/fbi-nsa-says-hacks-on-us-federal-agencies-likely-russian-in-origin\/\">the SolarWinds campaign<\/a> was &#8220;likely Russian in origin.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"KOWDaGB7FW\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/23\/solarwinds-hackers-targeted-nasa-federal-aviation-administration-networks\/\">SolarWinds hackers targeted NASA, Federal Aviation Administration networks<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;SolarWinds hackers targeted NASA, Federal Aviation Administration networks&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/23\/solarwinds-hackers-targeted-nasa-federal-aviation-administration-networks\/embed\/#?secret=KOWDaGB7FW\" data-secret=\"KOWDaGB7FW\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Microsoft is warning customers that a new China state-sponsored threat actor is exploiting four previously undisclosed security flaws in Exchange Server, an enterprise email product built by the software giant. tips for SaaS founders who don\u2019t want VC money"},"content":{"rendered":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"\/>\t<\/svg>\n\t\t\t\t<\/a>\n\t\t<\/div>\n\t\t\t<\/div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tAytekin Tank is the founder of <a href=\"https:\/\/www.jotform.com\/\">JotForm<\/a>, an online form builder. Established in 2006, JotForm allows customizable data collection for enhanced lead generation, survey distribution, payment collections and more.\t<\/div>\n\t\n\t<\/div>\n<\/div><p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Over the past<\/span> decade, venture capital has become synonymous with entrepreneurship. Founders from around the world arrive in Silicon Valley with visions of record-setting A rounds and billion-dollar valuations. But what if you don\u2019t have unicorn dreams \u2014 or you don\u2019t want to pursue VC money?<\/p>\n<p>Bootstrapping a SaaS company is not only possible \u2014 I believe it\u2019s a saner, more sustainable way to build and scale a business. To be clear, bootstrapping isn\u2019t always easy. It requires patience and focus, but the freedom to create a meaningful product, on your terms, is worth more than even the biggest VC check.<\/p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--left\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tThe freedom to create a meaningful product, on your terms, is worth more than even the biggest VC check.\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">I started my company,<\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/www.jotform.com\/\"> JotForm<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">, in 2006. We\u2019ve grown steadily from a simple web tool into a product that serves more than 8 million users \u2014 without taking a dime in outside funding. We\u2019re profitable in an industry with big-name competitors like Google.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Most importantly, I still love this company and its mission, and I want the same for my fellow entrepreneurs. If you\u2019re a SaaS founder who\u2019s wary of VC funding, here are my best bootstrapping tips.<\/p>\n<h2>Keep your day job<\/h2>\n<p>Success stories from founders who leap blindly into business without resources or relevant experience are compelling, but they\u2019re the exception, not the rule. Working inside another organization can build your skills, your network and even inspire great product ideas.<\/p>\n<p>After finishing college with a computer science degree, I worked as a developer for a New York media company. The editors always needed custom web forms, which were tedious and time consuming to build. I kept thinking, \u201cThere has to be a better way.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>That daily frustration led me to start JotForm \u2014 but I didn\u2019t leave my job right away. I stayed with the media firm for five years and worked on my product on the side. By the time I was ready to go all in, I had the confidence, experience and savings I needed.<\/p>\n<p>Many of the world\u2019s biggest companies began as side projects, including Twitter, Craigslist, Slack, Instagram, Trello, and a little venture called Apple. If your day job doesn\u2019t pay enough to fund the early stages of your business, consider a side gig or consulting work. There are so many ways to set yourself up for success without the pressure of VC cash or selling a chunk of your business.<\/p>\n<h2>Know you\u2019re not alone<\/h2>\n<p>The exact numbers shift every year, but data compiled by<a href=\"https:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/230011\"> Fundable<\/a> show that only 0.05% of U.S. startups are backed by VCs. Another 0.91% are funded by angel investors. The vast majority, at 57%, are funded by credit and personal loans, while 38% get funding from friends and family.<\/p>\n<p>It may feel like most founders raise multimillion-dollar rounds, but that\u2019s simply not the case. It\u2019s also good to remember that securing VC money is complicated and time consuming. You can spend months taking meetings and presenting the perfect deck \u2014 and still leave empty handed. Be patient and stick to your own path.<\/p>\n<h2>Measure profits, not popularity<\/h2>\n<p>SaaS founders often emphasize vanity metrics, like user acquisitions and total downloads. These numbers can measure short-term popularity, but they don\u2019t reveal how users and customers feel about your product \u2014 or your long-term potential.<div Equity","slug":"private-equity","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/29172"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=29172"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=29172"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=29172"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=29172"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[{"id":576796353,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/extracrunch\/fundraising\/","name":"Fundraising","slug":"fundraising","taxonomy":"tc_ec_category","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_ec_category\/576796353"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_ec_category"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_ec_category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_ec_category=576796353"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[]]}},{"id":2119915,"date":"2021-03-02T12:08:17","date_gmt":"2021-03-02T20:08:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119915"},"modified":"2021-03-02T13:03:13","modified_gmt":"2021-03-02T21:03:13","slug":"retail-zipline-series-b","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/retail-zipline-series-b\/","title":{"rendered":"Retail Zipline raises $30M as it helps retailers adapt to the pandemic"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">When I first wrote about <a href=\"https:\/\/www.retailzipline.com\">Retail Zipline<\/a> in 2019, the startup was focused on building a communication platform that would <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/16\/retail-zipline-series-a\/\">help corporate decision-makers in retail communicate with individual stores<\/a>. As you\u2019d probably guess, the startup saw some changes in 2020.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhen COVID first hit, you might think a company that\u2019s primarily focused on retail would be in trouble,\u201d said co-founder and CTO Jeremy Baker. \u201cBut it turns out that a product that helps retailers communicate critical information when everything is changing is no longer a nice to have.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In other words, where Retail Zipline might previously have been used for coordinating sales and promotions, it suddenly became a channel for managing things like health and safety protocols and communicating about furloughs and closures.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Co-founder and CEO Melissa Wong said the platform supports both engagement (a company executives sending a message to retail associates) and execution (translating a broader corporate strategy into an in-store experience). While you might think that execution was the only thing that mattered in the middle of a pandemic, Wong argued that the engagement side was also essential, particularly when employees felt they were putting themselves at risk.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe engagement part means that we can explain to a retail employee what we\u2019re doing to protect you during this crisis, and your role as part of this company and this brand,\u201d she said.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1828959\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1828959\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-1828959\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Retail Zipline screenshot\" width=\"680\" height=\"491\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg 2886w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=150,108 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=300,216 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=768,554 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=680,491 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=1536,1108 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=2048,1477 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Tablet-and-Phone-Landscape-2.jpg?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1828959\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Retail Zipline<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>She added that the company has doubled its customer baes during the pandemic and seen revenue increase 2.5x. Retailers using the platform include Sephora, AEO, L.L.Bean, Gap, Hy-Vee, Lush Cosmetics, BevMo, LL Flooring, Cole Haan, The LEGO Group, TOMS and Torrid.<\/p>\n<p>The pandemic also spurred dramatic growth in e-commerce, but Wong (who previously worked on the corporate side of Gap and Old Navy) suggested that this won\u2019t eliminate the need for physical stores. Instead, it just means they\u2019ll have to live up to the long-standing \u201comni-channel promise,&#8221; where they serve as both a store and a distribution center for online orders.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cRetail will become more complex,\u201d she said. \u201cWe will enable them to meet those complexities.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Today, Retail Zipline is announcing that it has raised $30 million in Series B funding. The round was led by real estate-focused firm Fifth Wall, with partner Dan Wenhold joining the board of directors. Emergence Capital, Ridge Ventures, Hillsven Capital, Veeva co-founder Matt Wallach and the Fisher Family Fund also participated.<\/p>\n<p>The company has now raised more than $39 million, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.crunchbase.com\/organization\/retail-zipline\">according to Crunchbase<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>In a blog post, Fifth Wall wrote:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>The Fifth Wall network is rich with opportunities for Zipline to explore potential partnerships among our retail-focused partners and portfolio companies. However, we believe retail to be just the beginning for Zipline as we envision the product appealing to many Built World industries. The opportunity for Zipline within real estate could lie with organizations whose HQ office must communicate daily with field operations workers, such as more traditional brokers with a geographic focus (e.g., CBRE, Cushman &amp; Wakefield), leasing agents within multifamily and SFR (e.g., Equity Residential, Greystar), or construction site workers.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5nFcXAdKXb\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/16\/retail-zipline-series-a\/\">Retail Zipline raises $9.6M from Emergence and Serena Williams<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Retail Zipline raises $9.6M from Emergence and Serena Williams&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/16\/retail-zipline-series-a\/embed\/#?secret=5nFcXAdKXb\" data-secret=\"5nFcXAdKXb\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premiere \u2018how-to\u2019 event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. GameOn app, a platform for sharing mobile gaming clips, launches on iOS"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Mobile gaming hasn&#8217;t seen the same demand for streaming content in the past as desktop has, but Amazon sees a market there to extend Twitch&#8217;s dominance. After launching on Android back in November, the company&#8217;s mobile streaming centric app has <a href=\"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/id1457912496\">just launched<\/a> on Apple&#8217;s App Store.<\/p>\n<p>The app lets users record short clips (anywhere from 30 seconds to 5 minutes of content) of gameplay from a variety of titles that support screen recording capture. Users can screen record these clips directly into the GameOn library at which point they can add commentary or additional edits before publishing to the GameOn platform or sharing links to the platform on other sites.<\/p>\n<p>The GameOn platform is interestingly fully disconnected from Twitch with separate branding and different channels. Amazon has been partnering with streamers to wholly focus on mobile gaming while promoting challenges unique to the app.The company says the service is compatible with over 1,000 mobile games.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Developers have been increasingly vigilant about brining more full-featured ports of desktop titles to mobile though the lack of sophisticated controls has made this a challenge. As gaming platforms aim to bring cloud streaming networks to iOS there could end up being more demand for shot-on-mobile content and titles that users control with a gamepad, but this will depend on whether the App Store grows more amenable to these platforms over time.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premier \u2018how-to\u2019 event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. You\u2019ll hear first-hand how some of the most successful founders and VCs build their businesses, raise money and manage their portfolios. We\u2019ll cover every aspect of company-building: Fundraising, recruiting, sales, legal, PR, marketing and brand building. Each session also has audience participation built-in \u2013 there\u2019s ample time included in each for audience questions and Tenth&#8217;s app encourages women to start home businesses, not join MLMs"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A new digital marketplace called <a href=\"https:\/\/www.westtenth.com\/\">West Tenth<\/a>, now backed by $1.5 million in seed funding, wants to give women a platform to start and grow their home-based businesses. Through its mobile app, women can promote their business to others in the local community, then field inquiries and requests through the app&#8217;s integrated messaging platform, as well as finalize transactions through in-app payments.<\/p>\n<p>The startup was co-founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/lwjohnson\/\">Lyn Johnson<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/lwjohnson\/\">Sara Sparhawk<\/a>, who met when they both worked in finance. Johnson remained in finance, but Sparhawk later moved on to work at Amazon.<\/p>\n<p>Johnson explains that her experience led her to better understand the economic inequality of women in the U.S., where they only own 32 cents to every dollar in financial assets than men own. A large driver of this is that women leave the workforce, often to raise children, which results in years where they don&#8217;t have earnings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re really good as a society at supporting women on the way of out of the workforce to care for their kids, but really terrible at supporting them on the way back in,&#8221; Johnson says. &#8220;Women know this, and as an alternative to employment that just seems to fail them, they&#8217;re starting businesses in droves.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119836\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119836\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2119836\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png 3600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-4.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119836\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> West Tenth<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>With <a href=\"https:\/\/www.westtenth.com\/\">West Tenth<\/a>, the goal is to encourage this sort of entrepreneurship &#8212; and more broadly, to help women understand that the many of the talents they&#8217;ve developed at home are, in fact, potential businesses.<\/p>\n<p>This includes opportunities like home-based bakers and cooks, photographers, home organizers or designers, home florists, baby sleep consultants, party planning and event services, crafting classes, fitness training, homemade goods, and more.<\/p>\n<p>The company notes that the app isn&#8217;t necessarily closed to men, but the current market for U.S. home businesses favors women as they&#8217;re more often the partner who chooses to leave work to raise children. However, there are some men on its platform.<\/p>\n<p>Though today many of these entrepreneurs market their home businesses on Facebook, they&#8217;re missing opportunities to reach customers if they&#8217;re not heavily involved in local groups and responding to requests for recommendations. West Tenth instead centralizes local businesses in one place to make discovery easier.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119843\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119843\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2119843\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png 3600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119843\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> West Tenth<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>In the app, customers can browse and shop local businesses, filtering by category via buttons at the top of the screen. The results are sorted by distance and offer photos, description, and the starting price for the goods or services offered. Through integrated messaging, users can reach out directly for a quote or more information. Customers can also complete their purchases through the app&#8217;s Stripe payments integration. West Tenth takes a 9.5% commission on these sales.<\/p>\n<p>Another key aspect to West Tenth is its education component, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.westtenth.com\/foundry\">The Foundry<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Through a $100 per quarter subscription membership (or $350 per year), business owners will be able to attend bi-monthly events, including classes focused on the fundamentals of setting up home-based businesses, marketing, customer acquisition, and other topics. These classes will also be available \u00e0 la carte at around $30 apiece, for those who want to pay per session.<\/p>\n<p>In addition, attendees will hear from guest speakers who have experience in the home-based business market, and they&#8217;ll be able join mastermind networking groups to exchange ideas with their peers.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119861\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119861\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2119861\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"585\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg 1954w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?resize=150,129 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?resize=300,258 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?resize=768,660 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?resize=680,585 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?resize=1536,1321 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-02-at-1.24.21-PM.jpg?resize=50,43 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119861\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> West Tenth<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>This system of combining education and networking with business ownership could potentially help more women become home-based business entrepreneurs instead of joining multi-level marketing (MLM) companies, as is common.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;When we started this, we recognized that MLMs are one of the few kind of industries that&#8217;s focused on this demographic of women who&#8217;ve left the workforce &#8212; which is a huge, untapped talent pool in the U.S.,&#8221; notes Johnson. &#8220;But they&#8217;re really predatory. Only the top 1% of sellers distributors really make money and the rest lose money. And they lose their social capital, as well. What we&#8217;re really interested in doing is becoming an alternative to MLMs in many respects,&#8221; she adds.<\/p>\n<p>Not surprisingly, MLMs aren&#8217;t allowed on the West Tenth platform.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119840\" style=\"width: 463px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119840\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2119840\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?w=453\" alt=\"\" width=\"453\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png 2400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=100,150 100w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=200,300 200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=768,1152 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=453,680 453w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=1024,1536 1024w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=1365,2048 1365w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-8.png?resize=33,50 33w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 453px) 100vw, 453px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119840\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> West Tenth<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The startup, which completed Kansas City TechStars last summer, has now raised $1.5 million in seed funding to get its platform off the ground. The round was led by Better Ventures along with Stand Together Ventures Lab, Kapital Partners,The Community Fund, Backstage Capital, Wedbush Ventures, and Gaingels.<\/p>\n<p>The funds will be used to develop the product and grow its user base. In time, West Tenth aims to build out product features to better highlight local businesses. This includes shopping elements that will let you see what friends are buying and video demonstrations, among other things.<\/p>\n<p>Since 2019, West Tenth has grown its footprint from just 20 businesses on the app to now over 600, largely in suburban L.A. and Salt Lake City. It&#8217;s now aiming to target growth in Phoenix, Boise, and Northern California.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119833\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119833\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2119833\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png 3600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-2.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119833\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> West Tenth<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The timing for West Tenth&#8217;s expansion is coming on the tail end of the COVID-19 crisis, where things have only gotten worse for women&#8217;s traditional employment.<\/p>\n<p>School and daycare closures combined with job losses that <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2020\/05\/09\/us\/unemployment-coronavirus-women.html\">greatly impacted women&#8217;s roles<\/a> have <a href=\"https:\/\/www.americanprogress.org\/issues\/women\/reports\/2020\/10\/30\/492582\/covid-19-sent-womens-workforce-progress-backward\/\">now driven more women out of the workforce<\/a> compared with men. And according to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.mckinsey.com\/industries\/public-and-social-sector\/our-insights\/achieving-an-inclusive-us-economic-recovery#\">McKinsey<\/a>, women accounted for nearly 56% of workforce exits since the start of the pandemic, despite making up just 48% of the workforce. This COVID-driven &#8220;<a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2020\/05\/09\/us\/unemployment-coronavirus-women.html\">shecession<\/a>,&#8221; as some have dubbed it, is also disproportionately impacting women of color, studies have found.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;ve seen 5 million women exit the workforce &#8212; some because they were laid off or furloughed, and a huge chunk because they&#8217;re opting out because the caregiving responsibilities just became overwhelming,&#8221; says Johnson.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The thing is when women leave the workforce for caregiving reasons &#8212; for some reason we really discount that and we make it even harder for them to return to work. So I think over the next 18 to 24 months, we&#8217;ll see a big surge in economic activity in the home with women trying to bring in additional sources of income by running a business from the home,&#8221; she says.<\/p>\n<p>The West Tenth app is available on both <a href=\"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/west-tenth\/id1478134804#?platform=iphone\">iOS<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/play.google.com\/store\/apps\/details?id=com.wtenth.w10\">Android<\/a>.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premiere \u2018how-to\u2019 event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. You\u2019ll hear first-hand how some of the most successful founders and VCs build their businesses, raise money and manage their portfolios. We\u2019ll cover every aspect of company-building: Fundraising, recruiting, sales, legal, PR, marketing and brand building. Each session also has audience participation built-in \u2013 there\u2019s ample time included in each for audience questions and discussion.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>\t<iframe\n\t\t\tid=\"wpcom-iframe-dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\twidth=\"99%\"\n\t\t\theight=\"1500\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https:\/\/tcprotectedembed.com\/protected-iframe\/dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\tscrolling=\"true\"\n\t\t\tframeborder=\"0\"\n\t\t\tclass=\"wpcom-protected-iframe\"\n\t>\n\t<\/iframe>\n\t<script re-apology-in-india-over-drama-series\/","title":{"rendered":"Amazon issues rare apology in India over drama series"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Amazon on Tuesday issued a rare apology to users in India for an original political drama series over allegations that a few scenes in the nine-part mini series hurt religious sentiments of some people in the key overseas market.<\/p>\n<p>The series, called \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/www.imdb.com\/title\/tt11117570\/\">Tandav<\/a>,\u201d has faced criticism from some people in India &#8212; including a few members of the ruling Bhartiya Janata Party &#8212; over its depiction of Hindu gods and goddesses.<\/p>\n<p>In a message titled, \u201cAmazon Prime Video Apologizes,\u201d the American e-commerce group said it \u201cdeeply regrets that viewers considered certain scenes to be objectionable\u201d and that it had either edited those scenes or removed them altogether from the show after hearing concerns from viewers.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe respect our viewers\u2019 diverse beliefs and apologize unconditionally to anyone who felt hurt by these scenes. Our teams follow company content evaluation processes, which we acknowledge need to be constantly updated to better serve our audiences. We will continue to develop entertaining content with partners, while complying with the laws of India and respecting the diversity of culture and beliefs of our audiences.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The show, which stars several top Bollywood actors including Saif Ali Khan, premiered in mid-January and immediately prompted\u00a0<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">controversy and criminal complaints. Things have escalated in recent weeks as several high-profile executives of Amazon Prime Video have been questioned by the authority.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Amazon Prime Video has been made to apologise. Sickening. <br \/>If you\u2019re offended by something, stop watching. Don\u2019t demand that it be scrubbed from existence. <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/hakPc1xqZ4\">pic.twitter.com\/hakPc1xqZ4<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Raja Sen (@RajaSen) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/RajaSen\/status\/1366762099863547904?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 2, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Prime Video has amassed millions of subscribers in India, where it competes with Disney&#8217;s Hotstar, Netflix, Times Internet&#8217;s MX Player, and dozens more streaming services. Amazon has grown more aggressive with Prime Video in India in recent months. It recently\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/amazon-launches-mobile-only-prime-video-subscription-in-india\/\">introduced an even cheaper subscription tier<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/scroll.in\/field\/978130\/cricket-amazon-prime-video-acquires-indian-territory-rights-for-all-matches-in-new-zealand\">secured rights<\/a> for streaming some cricket matches.<\/p>\n<p>Amazon\u2019s rare apology today comes days after New Delhi announced <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/25\/india-announces-sweeping-guidelines-for-social-media-on-demand-streaming-firms-and-digital-news-outlets\/\">new rules for on-demand video streaming services and social media firms<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Until now Amazon Prime Video and other streaming services have operated in India without having to worry too much about the nature of their content. But that\u2019s changing, according to the new rules.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe category classification of a content will take into account the potentially offensive impact of a film on matters such as caste, race, gender, religion, disability or sexuality that may arise in a wide range of works, and the classification decision will take account of the strength or impact of their inclusion,\u201d the new rules state.<\/p>\n<p>As we <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/25\/india-plays-hardball-with-amazon\/\">wrote recently<\/a>, the controversy surrounding the political drama and the new rules from India for streaming services are only few of the challenges that Amazon is facing in India, where it has <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/14\/amazon-to-invest-1-billion-to-digitize-small-businesses-in-india\/\">committed to deploy over $6.5 billion<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Last month, an influential India trader group that represents tens of millions of brick-and-mortar retailers <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/17\/indian-trader-group-calls-for-ban-on-amazon-following-dodging-regulations-claims\/\">called New Delhi to ban Amazon in the country<\/a> after an <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/investigates\/special-report\/amazon-india-operation\/\">investigation by Reuters<\/a> claimed that the American e-commerce group had given preferential treatment to a small group of sellers in India, publicly misrepresented its ties with those sellers and used them to circumvent foreign investment rules in the country.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"fFxTlC5cJw\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/24\/police-case-filed-against-netflix-executives-in-india-over-a-suitable-boy-kissing-scene\/\">Police case filed against Netflix executives in India over &#8216;A Suitable Boy&#8217; kissing scene<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Police case filed against Netflix executives in India over &#8216;A Suitable Boy&#8217;
